# LibreOffice Calc Formula Evaluation Chain

## Your Task

An on-call developer is investigating incorrect formula evaluation in LibreOffice Calc. Trace how a cell formula like `=SUM(A1:A10)` is parsed and evaluated. Find the key C++ source files in `LibreOffice/core` under `sc/` that implement the formula engine: 1. The file that implements the formula tokenizer/compiler (`sc/source/core/tool/compiler.cxx` or similar). 2. The file that implements `ScInterpreter` — the formula bytecode interpreter that evaluates formulas. 3. The file that defines `ScFormulaCell` — the cell type that holds a formula and its result. 4. The file that implements `ScRecalcMode` or recalculation scheduling — how Calc determines which cells need recalculation. Report each file path and key class/function.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/libreoffice-core--9c8b85f3` (LibreOffice/core)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully traced the LibreOffice Calc formula evaluation chain and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary of Findings

I've identified the key C++ source files implementing formula evaluation in LibreOffice Calc:

### **1. Formula Parsing (Compilation)**
- **File**: `sc/source/core/tool/compiler.cxx`
- **Class**: `ScCompiler` (defined in `sc/inc/compiler.hxx`)
- **Function**: Parses formula strings like `=SUM(A1:A10)` into token arrays

### **2. Formula Cell Storage**
- **Header**: `sc/inc/formulacell.hxx`
- **Implementation**: `sc/source/core/data/formulacell.cxx`
- **Class**: `ScFormulaCell`
- **Key Features**: Holds compiled token array, cached result, dirty flags, and position

### **3. Bytecode Interpreter**
- **Header**: `sc/source/core/inc/interpre.hxx`
- **Implementation**: `sc/source/core/tool/interpr*.cxx` (split across 8 files: interpr1-8.cxx)
- **Main Method**: `ScInterpreter::Interpret()` (at line 3976 in interpr4.cxx)
- **Function**: Executes the compiled bytecode and produces results

### **4. Recalculation Scheduling**
- **File**: `sc/inc/document.hxx`
- **Class**: `ScDocument`
- **Key Method**: `CalcFormulaTree()` - Triggers recalculation of dirty cells
- **Modes**: Defined in `include/formula/tokenarray.hxx` via `ScRecalcMode` enum

The evaluation chain flows from tokenization → storage → interpretation → result caching, with the document-level recalculation engine controlling which cells need evaluation based on dependency tracking and dirty flags.

The `Interpret()` method processes the token array sequentially\\n   - It maintains an evaluation stack for intermediate results\\n   - It handles function calls, operators, and cell references\\n   - Results are cached in the ScFormulaCell's `aResult` member\\n\\n4. **Recalculation Scheduling**: The recalculation process is controlled by:\\n   - `ScRecalcMode` enum (include/formula/tokenarray.hxx) specifying when formulas should recalculate (NORMAL, ALWAYS, ONLOAD_ONCE, etc.)\\n   - `ScDocument::CalcFormulaTree()` (sc/inc/document.hxx) which iterates through formula cells marked as dirty and triggers their `Interpret()` method\\n   - The formula cell's `bDirty` flag indicates whether recalculation is needed\\n   - Dependency tracking ensures that when a cell changes, all dependent cells are marked dirty\\n\\n5. **Group Evaluation**: For performance, consecutive formula cells with identical formulas (shared formulas) can be interpreted as a group via `ScFormulaCell::InterpretFormulaGroup()`, allowing vectorized operations where possible.\\n\\nThe key files implementing this chain are:\\n- sc/source/core/tool/compiler.cxx: Formula tokenization and parsing\\n- sc/source/core/inc/interpre.hxx + sc/source/core/tool/interpr*.cxx: Bytecode interpretation engine  \\n- sc/inc/formulacell.hxx + sc/source/core/data/formulacell.cxx: Formula cell container and evaluation orchestration\\n- include/formula/tokenarray.hxx: Recalculation mode definitions\\n- sc/inc/document.hxx: Document-level recalculation scheduling\"\n}\n",
